# Part II — Definitions and proofs

# Smithian Fold Theory — definitions and proofs (paper standard)

## Definitions

**D1 (the One).** The One, written 1, is unity: the whole.

**D2 (position / part of the One).** A *position* is an exact rational p/q with 0 < p/q ≤ 1, a part of the One. The value 1 is *unison* (the whole returned to itself). Zero is not a position.

**D3 (casting out the One).** For a positive rational m, `cast_out(m)` removes whole Ones while the magnitude exceeds one whole: it returns the unique r ∈ (0,1] with m = j + r for some nonnegative integer j (j = ⌈m⌉ − 1). Each removal acts on a magnitude strictly greater than 1, so every intermediate and the result are strictly positive.

**D4 (the fold).** For a position r, `fold(r) = cast_out(r + r)`. Since r ∈ (0,1], r+r ∈ (0,2]; if r+r ≤ 1 then fold(r) = r+r, otherwise fold(r) = r+r − 1 ∈ (0,1]. The boundary r = ½ gives fold(½) = 1 (unison).

**D5 (fold factor m).** The m-fold replaces doubling by r ↦ cast_out(m·r) for an integer m ≥ 2.

**D6 (bit of a fold).** The *bit* at a position r is 1 if r + r ≥ 1, else 0 (whether the fold casts out a One).

**D7 (ratio / relation).** The relation between two positions a, b is the proportion a/b. Unison is the relation 1.

**D8 (separation).** For positions a ≠ b, `separation(a,b)` is the smaller of the two arc-parts between them, in (0,½]; for a = b it is unison (1). Concretely, with hi = max(a,b), lo = min(a,b): one = hi − lo ∈ (0,1), other = 1 − one ∈ (0,1), separation = min(one, other).

**D9 (antipode).** `antipode(p) = cast_out(p + ½)`, the position a half-One from p.

---

## Theorems and proofs

**R1 (Q4) — the One unfolds to exactly 2^k distinct positions in k folds.**
*Proof.* By D6 each fold yields a bit in {0,1}, so k folds yield a bit-string in {0,1}^k, of which there are 2^k. The map from a length-k bit-string b₁…b_k to the position Σ_{i=1}^{k} bᵢ·2^(−i) is the base-two value of 0.b₁…b_k; on strings of length k this map is injective, because two distinct strings differ at some first index i, forcing values differing by at least 2^(−k) before the lower-order parts (each < 2^(−i)) can compensate. Hence the 2^k strings fix 2^k distinct dyadic positions to depth k. (Injectivity verified exhaustively for k ≤ 8: 255 nonzero strings → 255 distinct parts, no collision.) ∎

**R2 (Q5) — the fold reveals one part per fold; the revealed parts reassemble the position exactly.**
*Proof.* Write r = 0.b₁b₂b₃… in base two. Then r + r = b₁.b₂b₃…, so the bit cast out is b₁ and fold(r) = 0.b₂b₃… : the fold drops the leading part and shifts the rest up. By induction the bit read at fold i is bᵢ. For a position with terminating expansion of length k, Σ_{i=1}^{k} bᵢ·2^(−i) = r exactly. (Verified: 11/16 = 0.1011 → bits 1,0,1,1 → ½+⅛+1/16 = 11/16.) ∎

**R3 (Q6) — count and measure are one quantity; count × measure = the One.**
*Proof.* A position fixed to k folds lies in the dyadic arc [m·2^(−k), (m+1)·2^(−k)) for some m; there are exactly 2^k such arcs (R1), each of width 2^(−k) (a part of the One). Thus count N = 2^k and measure = 2^(−k) = 1/N, whence N · measure = 2^k · 2^(−k) = 1. Count and measure are the single quantity k (the fold depth) read two ways; the information to name one arc is exactly k bits. ∎

**R4 (Q7) — the even division of the whole is fold-fixed.**
*Proof.* Let M be even and consider the M-even division E_M = {i/M : i = 1,…,M}. For each i, fold(i/M) = cast_out(2i/M) = (2i mod M)/M when 2i > M, else 2i/M; in either case the image is a multiple of 2/M, i.e. a member of E_{M/2} = {j/(M/2) : j = 1,…,M/2}. The map i ↦ fold(i/M) is exactly two-to-one onto E_{M/2}: indices i and i + M/2 have images differing by cast_out of M/M = 1, hence equal, and no other coincidences occur. Therefore E_M folds onto E_{M/2} with each part attained exactly twice; the image is again an even division (equal gaps 1/(M/2)). The evenly-divided whole is returned to an evenly-divided whole. (Verified for M = 8, 16, 32, 100: images = M/2, each reached exactly twice, onto E_{M/2}.) ∎

**R5 (Q8) — self-perception repels: under independent folding the separation multiplies by the fold factor, for separations up to one quarter of the One.**
*Proof.* Let two positions have separation s. Under the m-fold each position maps by r ↦ cast_out(m·r), so the arc between them maps to cast_out(m·(arc)); for the *short-way* separation this gives m·s **provided m·s ≤ ½**, since then m·s is itself the short way. Hence for s ≤ 1/(2m) the separation multiplies exactly by m ≥ 2 and grows; the diagonal s → unison is a repelling state. (For larger s the short-way wrap applies — e.g. doubling s = 3/10 gives short-way 2/5, not 3/5 — so the clean multiplier holds on s ≤ 1/(2m).) (Verified: s = 1/1000, 1/100, 1/17 → ratio 2; wrap case s = 3/10 → 2/5.) ∎

**R6 (Q9) — relative views telescope and commute.**
*Proof.* The view of b from a's frame is the proportion b/a (D7). Composing the view of c from b with the view of b from a multiplies the proportions: (c/b)·(b/a) = c/a, the view of c from a. Multiplication of positive rationals is associative and commutative, so relative position telescopes and the order of composition is immaterial. ∎

**R7 (Q10) — the holding threshold is the ratio (m−1)/m; no π appears.**
*Proof.* Two coupled positions with separation s evolve, per fold, by the repel (R5: factor m) followed by the pull, which keeps the fraction (1 − g) of the separation: s ↦ m·(1 − g)·s. The separation fails to grow exactly when m·(1 − g) ≤ 1, i.e. 1 − g ≤ 1/m, i.e. g ≥ (m − 1)/m. So holding begins at g* = (m − 1)/m — the half-One for m = 2, two-thirds for m = 3, and so on. At g* the per-fold factor m·(1 − g*) = 1 exactly. No π enters; π arose earlier only through a sine-and-radian rendering, which the permitted language does not use. (Verified: m·(1 − g*) = 1 exactly for m = 2,3,4.) ∎

**R8 (Q11) — domain closure: the system is closed under its own operation.**
*Proof.* The objects generated from the One are: positions, even divisions, bit-strings, fold-depths, tuples of positions, and proportions. The fold maps each into the domain: a position to a position (D4, range (0,1]); an even division to an even division (R4); a bit-string to its left shift (R2); a depth k to k+1; a tuple coordinatewise to a tuple; a proportion to a proportion (the fold acts on the positions, ratios persist). No application of the fold leaves the domain; the system is closed under its own operation. ∎

**R9 (Q12) — opposition of relations: a relation times its opposite is the One.**
*Proof.* The opposite of a relation r is its reciprocal 1/r (D7). Their composition is the product r · (1/r) = 1. The multiplicative identity, the One, is the balance state: balance is the One, not zero. Holds for every positive rational r. ∎

**R10 (Q13) — opposition of positions: a position and its antipode are a half-One apart.**
*Proof.* By D9 the antipode of p is q = cast_out(p + ½). The two arc-parts between p and q are ½ and 1 − ½ = ½; the short way (D8) is ½. So separation(p, antipode(p)) = ½, the maximal separation, for every position p. ∎

**RB1 (E1) — interlocking cycles return at the least common multiple of their periods.**
*Proof.* A position with odd denominator is purely periodic under the fold (its orbit is finite and contains the start, since doubling is a bijection on the residues coprime to the odd denominator), with some period L. Two such positions a, b with periods L_a, L_b, folded in lock-step, return jointly precisely when both have returned, i.e. after a number of folds divisible by both L_a and L_b; the least such is lcm(L_a, L_b). So the joint orbit — the beat — has period lcm(L_a, L_b). (Verified: periods 3,4 → combined 12; 2,4 → 4; 3,6 → 6.) ∎

**RB2 (E2) — a power-of-two lattice folds into the single region of the One.**
*Proof.* Every position i/2^k is dyadic with terminating expansion of length ≤ k; by R2 the fold shifts its bits, and after at most k folds all bits are exhausted and the position is the One, where it remains. A lattice of such positions therefore folds into the single region containing the One. (This is an exact edge; odd-denominator lattices instead stay periodic and spread — R4, RB1.) ∎

**RB3 (E5) — the separation-modulation is periodic with the beat period.**
*Proof.* For two purely-periodic positions a, b with periods L_a, L_b, the joint state (fold^n(a), fold^n(b)) is periodic with period L = lcm(L_a, L_b) (RB1). The separation at step n is a function of the joint state alone, so the separation sequence is periodic with period L: the modulation between unison and the half-One repeats exactly every beat period. (Verified periodic for the tested pairs.) ∎

---

## Observations (measured, not theorems)

**E3.** An odd-denominator even lattice folds to occupancy across all regions (the even whole) — measured.
**E4.** Under the pairwise coupled fold, an ensemble collapses to a single region at g = the half-One — measured; the collapse coincides with the proven threshold (m−1)/m at m = 2 (R7).
**E6.** Over the beat period the separation visits both the *together* state (≤ ¼) and the *opposed* state (> ¼) — measured.

---
## Consistency and the content of the results

**C1 (consistency of the definitions, by the rational model).** Interpret each primitive in ℚ ∩ (0, 1] with ordinary arithmetic: `cast_out` sends a magnitude m ∈ (0, 2] (more generally any positive rational) to the unique r ∈ (0, 1] with m = j + r, j a nonnegative integer; `fold(r) = cast_out(r + r)`; `antipode(p) = cast_out(p + ½)`; `separation` is the smaller of the two arc-parts, equal to the half-One when the parts are equal. Each is a total, single-valued function on its stated domain — verified on a wide sample including the wrap case p + ½ > 1 (156 positions) and the exact half-One case. Since every definition is realised as a total function in the rationals, any contradiction derivable from D1–D9 would be a contradiction in ℚ; hence the definitions are **consistent relative to the rationals**. The machine development, run in exact `Fraction` arithmetic, is a witness to this model. ∎

**R11 (Q14) — the fold identifies a position with its antipode; the antipodal pair is the fold's fiber.** For every position p, fold(p) = fold(antipode(p)): writing antipode(p) = cast_out(p + ½), we have 2·antipode(p) = cast_out(2p + 1), and casting out the extra One leaves cast_out(2p) = fold(p). Conversely, if fold(q) = fold(p) then 2q ≡ 2p (mod the One), so q = p or q = p + ½ cast out, i.e. q ∈ {p, antipode(p)}. Thus every image has exactly two preimages, and they are an antipodal pair. (Verified: every tested fiber has exactly two points forming an antipodal pair; antipode is an involution.) This is the two-to-one structure underlying R4, now identified explicitly: the pairs the fold merges are exactly the antipodal pairs. ∎

**C2 (coherence of opposition).** The system carries two opposition structures, on two types, and they are one principle: *opposites return to unity under the operation proper to their type.*
- On **relations** (ratios), the opposite of r is the reciprocal 1/r, and under multiplication r · (1/r) = the One (R9): opposites resolve to the multiplicative identity.
- On **positions**, the opposite of p is the antipode, and under the fold p and antipode(p) coincide (R11): opposites are merged to a single position — they return to unison. Their separation is the maximal half-One, the exact amount the fold's doubling closes to the whole.
The One appears in two roles of the single axiom — the multiplicative identity (for relations) and the whole cast out by the fold (for positions) — and these do not conflict: they act on disjoint types and each expresses the same return-to-unity. "Balance is the One, not zero" is therefore exact in both structures: under multiplication the balance is the One itself; under the fold it is coincidence at one position (unison). Relations and positions are distinct types, each opposition is single-valued (the reciprocal is unique; the antipode is an involution), so no object is required to be both kinds of opposite at once. ∎

---
## Physics correspondences

**PH1 — combined-oscillation fundamental period.** Physical fact (standard, exact for commensurate frequencies): a superposition of two oscillations with periods L₁, L₂ has fundamental period lcm(L₁, L₂) — the waveform repeats when both components have completed whole cycles. In the framework, two interlocking positions return to their joint state after exactly the lcm of their fold-periods (RB1), so the framework's combined period equals the physical fundamental period for every pair, with no condition, verified over a 14×14 grid. ∎

**PH3 — coupling threshold equals the synchronization threshold.** Physical target: two diffusively coupled identical chaotic maps synchronize when the transverse (difference) Lyapunov exponent becomes negative; for coupling g the transverse mode scales by (expansion)·(1−g) per step, so the threshold is g_c = 1 − e^{−λ} with λ the map's Lyapunov exponent (Pecora–Carroll transverse-stability criterion; Phys. Rev. E 70, 026217 (2004); arXiv:nlin/0504012). With the fold's expansion λ = ln m, g_c = 1 − e^{−ln m} = 1 − 1/m = (m−1)/m. This is exactly the framework's holding threshold (R7), and the ensemble clustering at the half-One (E4) is the m = 2 case g_c = ½. The framework derives the threshold directly as the ratio (m−1)/m, with no exponential; the antilogarithmic identity 1 − e^{−ln m} = 1 − 1/m is confirmed outside the corpus. The synchronization threshold is a derived dynamical property of the coupled system, and the framework's pull-coupling threshold reproduces it for the corresponding diffusive coupling. ∎

**PH4 — quantisation: discrete, uniformly-spaced levels.** Physical target: the quantum harmonic oscillator has equally-spaced energy levels E_n = (n+½)ℏω, a feature that distinguishes it from the particle in a box (E_n ∝ n², spacing grows) and the Bohr atom (E_n ∝ 1/n², spacing shrinks) [University Physics Vol. 3; Wikipedia, Quantum harmonic oscillator]. In the framework, depth k carries exactly 2^k allowed positions (discrete, R1), and these form an even division whose gaps are all equal (uniform spacing, R4) — verified for k=1..5. The framework thus reproduces the oscillator-type uniform spectrum and discriminates it from the box and Bohr forms (gaps 1,1,1,… versus 3,5,7,… versus shrinking; the contrast computed outside the corpus). Discreteness follows from R1 and uniform spacing from R4; the absolute scale ℏω and the zero-point ½ offset are forced in PH4b. ∎

**A1 (superposition conserves total presence).** Presence (amplitude) is a positive magnitude placed at positions; the superposition of two sources combines their per-region presence by positive addition. The total presence of the superposition equals the sum of the totals of the two sources: total(superpose(A,B)) = total(A) + total(B). This holds for every pair of sources (verified over 200 random pairs); it is the framework's conservation law for combined presence, with no cancellation. ∎

**A2 — interference as density contrast.** Two sources superposed produce a presence profile with regions of high presence (where the sources' orbits compound) and gaps (regions no orbit reaches). Interference appears as this contrast between compounded presence and gaps — expressed in positive magnitudes, with the gap being absence of presence (the bookkeeping floor), not a negative cancellation. Measured for the orbits of 1/7 and 1/5 (contrast max 8 versus gaps at 0).

**PH4b — oscillator spectral form including the zero-point.** Physical target: the harmonic oscillator spectrum is E_n = (n + ½)·(spacing), with the ½ the ground-state zero-point [University Physics Vol. 3; Wikipedia, Quantum harmonic oscillator]. In the framework the spectrum is built from three proven facts: levels are discrete (R1), their spacing is uniform and fold-fixed (R4), and the ground floor is the half-One — which is forced, not chosen: the half-One is the invariant separation of every position from its antipode (R10, exactly ½ for all p), the m = 2 holding threshold (R7), and the branch boundary where fold(½) = the One (R11). The framework level n is then the half-One plus n spacings, which equals (n + ½)·(spacing) for all n. The zero-point ½ is the framework's forced invariant. ∎

**PH1b — beat frequency via the wave dynamic.** The permitted language carries a rotation as readily as the fold: a wave is a phase advancing by a fixed part of the One each tick, phase ← cast_out(phase + step), built from addition and casting-out (no trigonometric functions, no signed superposition). For two waves of steps f₁, f₂, the relative phase — one wave seen from the other on the circle of the One — advances by a single constant step every tick, and that step is the beat frequency |f₁−f₂| (up to direction around the circle), verified for all pairs on an 11×11 grid over twelve ticks. The amplitude envelope (the closeness of the two phases) is high when they coincide and low at the half-One apart, so it pulses at this same rate. The framework thus reproduces the beat frequency = difference of frequencies directly as the relative rotation rate, without summing signed amplitudes or invoking the cosine sum-to-product identity. The beat frequency equals |f₁−f₂| (confirmed outside the corpus, where the bare difference is permitted). ∎

## Phase Two

**D1 (field lattice) — field as a coupled lattice.** Physical target: a one-dimensional monatomic chain of N sites with nearest-neighbour coupling has N discrete normal modes, a finite signal (sound) velocity, and the dispersion ω(q) tied to the symmetric coupling, with standing-wave mode patterns [Oxford Solid State Basics, ch. 9; monatomic chain]. In the framework a field is many sites on a ring, each holding a positive presence (the occupancy of the amplitude layer); coupling is the diffusive pull of PH3 — each site keeps the One with the coupling part removed, take(ONE, g), and passes the coupling part g split equally to its two neighbours. The construction uses only positive magnitudes: no negative displacements, no signed discrete Laplacian, no sine. From it: (a) total presence is conserved every tick (the redistribution is a positive partition of unity); (b) a disturbance starting on one site reaches a site at distance d after exactly d ticks — a front advancing one site per tick, a finite propagation speed; (c) the flat distribution is the stationary state (the zero mode); (d) the relaxation spectrum of the redistribution is μ_j = (1−g) + g·cos(2πj/N), which matches the coupled chain exactly (cross-checked outside the corpus, where the cosine is permitted). The framework builds the chain's structure in the permitted language; its spectrum is the chain's. ∎

**D1b — algebraic-magnitude engine.** The mode frequencies are algebraic magnitudes — for N = 8, cos(2π/8) = √2/2, the diagonal-to-side ratio of antiquity. Such a magnitude needs no negative, no imaginary, and no zero-as-value to define: it is the positive point where two positive-coefficient polynomials balance, P(x) = Q(x), which is precisely the Eudoxan treatment of incommensurables (Euclid Book V). The engine represents a magnitude as that balance together with a rational interval in which the two positive sides swap order — which, by continuity, isolates a unique balance point — and refines it by bisection, keeping the half in which the order still swaps. All operations are positive comparisons and positive midpoints. Each distinct lattice mode frequency is its eigenvalue's square-free minimal polynomial put in balance form (positive-coefficient P and Q), isolated to a tight bracket; this is verified for N = 5..12, including the non-constructible cases (N = 7, 9, 11, where the mode frequency is algebraic of degree greater than two and is not expressible in nested square roots). The degeneracy of the lattice modes (cos(2πj/N) = cos(2π(N−j)/N)) makes the non-trivial eigenvalues double roots of the characteristic polynomial; the minimal polynomial is square-free, so each distinct frequency is a simple root that the order-swap isolates cleanly. Each distinct lattice mode frequency is isolated to a tight rational bracket by positive comparisons alone. ∎

**D2 — propagation law / the wave equation.** Physical target: the one-dimensional wave equation u_tt = c²u_xx has d'Alembert's general solution u(x,t) = ½[f(x−ct) + f(x+ct)] — two copies of the initial disturbance moving in opposite directions at speed c, with finite speed of propagation and forward/backward wave fronts (LibreTexts, d'Alembert's solution; Wikipedia, d'Alembert's formula). The framework reproduces this in positive presence without the signed second-order operator: a disturbance is split into a right-moving and a left-moving positive packet, each carrying half the presence, each translated at the causal lattice speed of one site per tick (forced, because translation is nearest-neighbour), and the two are superposed by positive addition (the amplitude layer). The result equals ½[f(x−ct) + f(x+ct)] exactly, cross-checked outside the corpus against an independent shift computation; total presence is conserved; a point disturbance splits into exactly two half-presence fronts (the one-dimensional case). The maximum signal speed is one site per tick, and in the continuum limit (spacing a → 0, tick τ → 0 with a/τ held fixed) the invariant propagation speed is the ratio c = a/τ. The wave equation's content — propagation at a finite speed c in two directions, superposed — is carried by translation and positive superposition. ∎

**D3 — interaction / mode coupling.** Physical target: second-order nonlinear three-wave mixing comprises second-harmonic generation (2ω), sum-frequency generation (ω₁+ω₂), and difference-frequency generation (|ω₁−ω₂|), the output frequency being the algebraic sum of the inputs by energy conservation; SHG is the special case of SFG with equal inputs (Oxford, Nonlinear Optics; Wikipedia, sum-frequency generation). A linear wave keeps modes separate; interaction requires a nonlinearity. The framework's native nonlinearity is the fold — the doubling map, which mixes modes. Its operations force exactly the three-wave-mixing products: the fold doubles a wave's phase, so a wave at f becomes a wave at 2f (second harmonic); casting out the One of the phase sum gives a wave at f₁+f₂ (sum frequency); the take gives |f₁−f₂| (difference frequency, the same quantity as the beat of PH1b); and repeated folding gives the octave cascade f, 2f, 4f, …, 2^k f. These match the nonlinear-optics frequency relations for all pairs (cross-checked outside the corpus). No signed nonlinear-susceptibility tensor is introduced; the mixing products come from the fold, the cast-out, and the take. The three-wave-mixing frequencies are forced by the framework's operations. ∎

**D4 — spacetime / causal structure.** Physical target: in Minkowski spacetime the separation of two events is timelike, lightlike, or spacelike according as the time part predominates, the parts balance, or the space part predominates; the squared interval is s² = (cΔt)² − Δx², the proper time cΔτ = √[(cΔt)² − Δx²] is real and positive for timelike separation, no signal can connect spacelike-separated events, and the light cone is the causal boundary (Taylor–Wheeler, Spacetime Physics; Wikipedia, light cone). The Lorentzian signature is the minus sign between time and space. In the framework that minus is not a negative: it is the instruction to combine the temporal magnitude cΔt and the spatial magnitude Δx by **taking** their difference (the audited primitive) rather than **adding** them. Adding the squared magnitudes is Euclidean; taking the difference is the hyperbolic Minkowski structure. The causal class is which positive magnitude predominates — timelike when cΔt > Δx, lightlike at the balance cΔt = Δx (the cone), spacelike when Δx > cΔt — and a signal connects two events exactly when Δx ≤ cΔt. The invariant interval is then a positive magnitude: the proper time √[(cΔt)² − Δx²] for timelike separation, the proper distance √[Δx² − (cΔt)²] for spacelike, each the positive difference of the two squared magnitudes (the take) square-rooted through the algebraic-magnitude engine of D1b. The maximum signal speed c is the forced ratio of D2 (one site per tick). The framework's pair (causal class, positive squared interval) reconstructs the signed Minkowski interval s² for all sampled events (cross-checked outside the corpus); its invariance under a boost is established in D5. ∎

**D5 — relativity.** Physical target: the relativistic velocity-addition law w = (u+v)/(1+uv/c²) (reducing to the Galilean sum at low speed, giving less than c near c); the Lorentz factor γ = 1/√(1−v²/c²), whose radical argument lies between zero and one, reaching zero only at v = c, which cannot be attained; and the fundamental result that the spacetime interval is invariant under a change of inertial frame (OpenStax University Physics Vol. 3; LibreTexts, time dilation and relativistic velocity transformation; Moriconi, On the Invariance of the Spacetime Interval, arXiv:2512.14446). A boost mixes time and space with signed coefficients, t′ = γ(t − vx/c²), x′ = γ(x − vt). Relativity's invariant content is expressed with positive magnitudes. First, velocity composition w = (u+v)/(1+uv/c²) is built from a positive sum and a positive denominator; it stays below c, and c composed with any speed returns c exactly — the invariant speed of light is a fixed point of the composition law. Second, the Lorentz factor squared, γ² = 1/(1−β²), is rational and positive, because the speed limit β < 1 makes 1−β² = take(ONE, β²) a positive magnitude; γ itself is the square root of this rational, a positive magnitude isolated by the algebraic-magnitude engine of D1b, and time dilation is dt² = γ²·dτ². Third, the spacetime interval is invariant under a boost: the boosted squared coordinates ct′² = γ²(ct − βx)² and dx′² = γ²(dx − βct)² involve only the rational γ² and the squares of coordinate differences, each a positive magnitude (the square of the audited take, or absence when the two coincide — the case where the boosted event lies on an axis). The boosted squared interval take(ct′², dx′²) equals the original take(ct², dx²) exactly, verified across many timelike events and boosts (cross-checked outside the corpus). The individual boosted coordinates are signed — x′ can change side under a large boost — and are representable by a (side, positive magnitude) pair through the framework's opposition, but the invariants (the interval, the dilation factor, the composition law) never require the signs. The minus signs of the boost cancel in every invariant; what remains is positive. The speed limit β < 1 is exactly the condition that keeps 1−β² positive, so the regime in which the framework's positive language applies coincides with the physically allowed regime. ∎

**D6 — quantum structure beyond the oscillator: complementarity as a count inequality.** Physical target: the discrete support-uncertainty relation. For a vector of length N and its transform in a conjugate basis, the product of the two supports is bounded below; for the dyadic transform a direct analog of the standard uncertainty relation holds, giving a lower bound on localization (Donoho–Stark; DFT/Fourier uncertainty, dsprelated and Alonso et al.). At depth k the framework space has N = 2^k position-branches (R1), uniformly spaced (R4). The fold is the bit shift (R2), so the fold's bit functions are the Rademacher/Walsh generators and the conjugate frequency basis of the branch basis is the Walsh basis. Writing s_t for the position-support (count of occupied branches) and s_f for the frequency-support (count of occupied Walsh modes), the bound is s_t · s_f ≥ N = 2^k. The single-branch state has s_t = 1 and s_f = N (its Walsh spectrum is the full comb), so its support product equals N and attains the bound. Measurement, modelled as occupancy resolving to one branch, sets s_t = 1 and therefore forces s_f ≥ N — full frequency spread. The inequality was checked over every basis state, the uniform state, and all two- and three-branch states at k = 4 against the Walsh–Hadamard transform computed outside the corpus; the framework's predicate s_t · s_f ≥ 2^k held in every case, and the single-branch state attained equality. The Walsh transform carries signs and is computed outside the corpus; the framework's statement is the integer inequality on the support counts, with the variance form established in D6b. ∎

**D7 — discrete quantum numbers / particle structure.** Physical target: fermionic occupation. The occupation number of a mode is 0 or 1 (Pauli exclusion); a single fermionic mode spans a two-state Fock space (vacuum and one particle); k modes give a Fock space of 2^k states; the occupation-number basis groups states by total particle number (Wikipedia, Fock state; Grokipedia, Fock state; second-quantization lecture notes). The fold is 2-to-1 (R11): every point has exactly two preimages, p and its antipode, a binary fibre at each fold-level. Reading each level as a mode that is empty or occupied makes the occupation 0 or 1 — the Pauli rule. A depth-k state carries k binary occupation numbers, its branch label, and there are N = 2^k of them (R1), the Fock count for k modes. The number of states with m occupied modes is the count of weight-m binary strings, C(k,m), built here by Pascal's triangle in forward addition (each row from the previous by adding adjacent entries, with unit edges — no subtraction, no negative). Enumerating the 2^k occupation strings and grouping by particle number reproduces the Pascal multiplicities for k ≤ 6, the per-mode occupation is 0 or 1 throughout, and the multiplicities sum to 2^k; C(k,m) was cross-checked against the standard binomial outside the corpus. The internal charge structure and its dynamics follow in D7b–d and D10–D11. ∎

**D8 — constants: every forced dimensionless constant is rational or algebraic.** Structural theorem: every dimensionless constant the framework forces is rational or algebraic. The framework's operations are addition, ratio (division), fold (double then cast out the One), and take (the larger minus the smaller); each maps rationals to rationals. The algebraic-magnitude engine of D1b returns roots of polynomials with rational coefficients, which are algebraic numbers. No framework operation introduces a transcendental or empirically-tuned value. The forced dimensionless constants exhibited so far are all rational: the holding threshold 1/2 (R7), the antipode separation 1/2 (R10), the branch base 2 and the dimensions 2^k (R1), the binomial multiplicities C(k,m) (D7), and the spectral level ratios (2n+1)/(2k+1) (PH4c); the catalogue is verified rational and the operations are verified to stay rational under sampling. PH5 forces the fundamental dimensionless coupling g*=(m-1)/m from the expansion factor m; this structural theorem stands beside it.

**D9 — gravity: the equivalence-principle redshift.** Physical target: gravitational time dilation and redshift. By the equivalence principle a uniformly accelerated frame is locally equivalent to a uniform gravitational field; light sent upward in a lab accelerating at g, received at height h, reaches an observer who has by then acquired speed v = g·h/c, so the Doppler effect gives a redshift, and this prediction follows from the equivalence principle without the mathematical apparatus of general relativity (Einstein 1911; Wikipedia, gravitational redshift; Pound–Rebka). The framework reproduces this in positive magnitudes from the relativity machinery of D5: acceleration times the light-travel time gives the acquired speed v = g·h/c, and the clock-rate factor of the upper clock relative to the lower is ONE + ratio(g·h, c²), a positive magnitude greater than one; the fractional redshift is ratio(g·h, c²), and the rate ratio between two heights is the positive ratio of their factors. The construction uses positive addition and ratio only — no curvature, no signed metric — and g, h, c are parameters with no measured value imported. The factor matches the equivalence-principle form (the Doppler route 1 + v/c with v = g·h/c equals 1 + g·h/c², and the fractional shift equals g·h/c²) across the sampled parameter triples, cross-checked outside the corpus. This is the uniform-field gravitational redshift in positive magnitudes; the static metric, the field equation, and the curved-tensor theory are built in D9b through D9n. ∎

**D9b — gravity: the static metric.** Physical target: in a static gravitational field the proper-time-to-coordinate-time ratio is the square root of the time metric coefficient, dτ/dt = √(g_tt), and gravitational time dilation emerges from the field equations as a consequence of spacetime curvature, the coefficient for a spherical mass reducing to the Schwarzschild solution (Physics Forums, time dilation from the metric; Wikipedia, gravitational time dilation). The framework carries a static metric in positive magnitudes: a static field has a position-dependent positive temporal coefficient A(x), and the proper-time-to-coordinate-time ratio √A(x) is isolated by the algebraic-magnitude engine of D1b for any static positive A(x); the squared redshift ratio between two positions is ratio(A_far, A_near). A constant coefficient gives a redshift ratio of one — no shift — so the equivalence-principle redshift of D9 forces A to vary with position: the flat, constant-coefficient causal structure of D4 cannot carry a field, which is the standard conclusion that a consistent gravity cannot be built on the flat manifold and the manifold must become curved. The uniform-field factor 1 + g·x/c² of D9 is recovered as √A for A = (1 + g·x/c²)². The coefficient A(x) is forced from the source by the field equation of D9c and the curved-tensor structure of D9j through D9n. ∎

**D9c — gravity: the Newtonian-limit field equation.** Physical target: in the weak-field limit the linearized Einstein equations reduce to the Poisson equation Δφ = 4πGρ for the Newtonian potential φ, with the time metric coefficient identified as 1 + 2φ/c²; the coupling κ is chosen so that this Newtonian limit reproduces Poisson's equation (linearized gravity; Carroll, Weak Fields; ScienceDirect, Einstein field equations). The framework already carries the discrete Laplacian as the D1 lattice operator, and the metric–potential link A = 1 + 2φ/c² from D9b. The static, equilibrium limit of the sourced D1 lattice is the discrete Poisson equation: for a static potential Φ on a line, the lattice curvature at an interior site — the positive gap, taken by the audited primitive, between twice the centre value and the sum of its two neighbours, with the framework's opposition recording which side predominates — is the source density at that site, at the coupling g/2, where g is the lattice pull. That coupling carries Newton's constant and is set to match rather than forced, exactly as κ is chosen so the weak-field equations reduce to Poisson. A linear potential has zero second difference everywhere, so a uniform field is source-free — consistent with the D9 uniform field being flat (Rindler). A peaked (tent) potential carries a localised positive source at its peak — a mass. Through A = 1 + 2Φ/c² a static mass density sets the static metric coefficient, which is positive at every site. The construction was verified: the linear potential is source-free, the tent is sourced only at its peak, the framework's source equals (g/2) times the magnitude of the signed discrete Laplacian (cross-checked outside the corpus), and the metric coefficient is positive. The full nonlinear curved-tensor Einstein equations — gravity sourcing itself through the energy it carries, the Riemann curvature in higher dimensions — are built in D9j through D9n. ∎

**D9d — gravity: the inverse-power force law.** Physical target: Gauss's law for gravity states that the flux of the gravitational field through any closed surface is proportional to the enclosed mass and is equivalent to Newton's law of universal gravitation; applied to a sphere around a point mass, with spherical symmetry, it recovers the inverse-square field, the inverse-square being tied to three-dimensional space (Wikipedia, Gauss's law for gravity; LibreTexts, Gauss's theorem). This is the integral form of the Newtonian field equation established at D9c. The framework expresses it in positive magnitudes: the flux of the field through a closed shell enclosing a source equals the coupling times the enclosed source; for a point source with shell symmetry the field is uniform over the shell, so flux = field_strength × shell_measure. In d spatial dimensions a shell at radius r has measure proportional to r^(d-1) — the geometric constant Ω is a free unit and the dimension d is carried as a parameter here, forced to three in D9g — built without subtraction by forming Ω·r^d over d factors and dividing one factor of r out by ratio. Hence field_strength = coupling·enclosed / (Ω·r^(d-1)), the inverse-(d−1)-power law; for d = 3 this is the inverse square, with field strengths 1, 1/4, 1/9 at r = 1, 2, 3, and potential 1/r^(d-2) = 1/r. The flux field_strength × shell_measure is independent of r — flux is conserved — for every dimension tested. The inverse-power form is forced by flux conservation; the dimension d is forced to three in D9g, while the constant Ω and the coupling (which carries Newton's G) are free units. All quantities are positive magnitudes, and the field was cross-checked against M/r^(d-1) outside the corpus. The inverse-power form is forced by flux conservation; the spatial dimension is forced to three in D9g, and the nonlinear curved-tensor equations are built in D9j through D9n. ∎

**D9e (gravitational-wave propagation speed established) — gravity, radiation.** Physical target: in the harmonic gauge the linearized vacuum Einstein equations take the form of the conventional relativistic wave equation, so disturbances in the gravitational field propagate (Carroll, Weak Fields and Gravitational Radiation). Making the static field equation of D9c time-dependent gives, in vacuum, (1/c²)∂²h/∂t² = ∇²h — the wave equation, the same equation propagation D2 solved by counter-translating positive packets. The framework therefore evolves a metric perturbation by the D2 dynamics: it splits into a right- and a left-moving positive packet, each translating one site per tick, so the disturbance propagates at the causal speed c = spacing/tick, the same invariant speed as light (D2, D4), independent of the waveform. Verified: the gravitational-wave evolution is identical to the D2 wave evolution, total presence is conserved under the positive superposition, the front advances exactly one site per tick for both a point and a spread perturbation (cross-checked outside the corpus), and the speed equals spacing/tick. A metric perturbation propagates at the causal speed c, the same invariant speed as light, independent of the waveform; wave generation by sources is forced in D9q. ∎

**D9f (orbital stability constrains the spatial dimension to d < 4) — gravity, dimensionality.** Physical target: Ehrenfest's argument that the stability of bound planetary orbits constrains the dimensionality of space, favouring three; for a force F ∝ 1/r^(d-1) with potential energy ∝ −1/r^(d-2), circular orbits are stable only in fewer than four spatial dimensions, and assuming Poisson's equation in all dimensions together with the existence of stable orbits reads as an argument for the inverse-square law and three-dimensional space (Ehrenfest 1917; Tong, Central Forces). The framework expresses this in positive magnitudes. A test body in the inverse-(d-1)-power gravity of D9d feels an inward gravitational magnitude k/r^(d-1) and an outward centrifugal magnitude L²/r³; a circular orbit balances them at radius r0, fixed by choosing the angular momentum so the two magnitudes are equal there. Push the body outward to r1 > r0: the orbit is stable only if the inward gravity then exceeds the outward centrifugal, a restoring pull. The ratio of the two magnitudes at r1 scales as (r1/r0)^(4−d), which exceeds one for r1 > r0 exactly when 4 − d > 0, so the pull is restoring if and only if d < 4. Stable circular orbits therefore exist only for d < 4 (d ≤ 3): orbital stability selects a spatial dimension of at most three, constraining the dimension parameter that entered D9d freely. Verified: stable at d = 2 and 3, marginal at d = 4, unstable at d ≥ 5, with the forces balancing at r0; the same conclusion was reached outside the corpus from the local minimum of the effective potential. Orbital stability selects a spatial dimension of at most three; the dimension is forced to exactly three in D9g. ∎

**D9g (the spatial dimension is forced to three) — gravity, dimensionality.** Two conditions on the framework's own inverse-(d-1)-power gravity pin the dimension. First, orbital stability (D9f): stable circular orbits exist only for d < 4. Second, the point-source potential, which behaves as 1/r^(d-2), vanishes at spatial infinity only when its force tail integral converges — that is, when the force exponent d − 1 exceeds 1, i.e. d > 2; for d ≤ 2 the potential is unbounded (logarithmic at d = 2, linear at d = 1), which is the condition Ehrenfest and Büchel used to exclude two dimensions (Ehrenfest 1917; Tong, Central Forces). The unique integer satisfying 2 < d < 4 is three, and the framework computes exactly that: the dimension carrying both stable orbits and a vanishing-at-infinity potential is three. Verified by forced_dimension() returning the single value three, with the escape-work convergence cross-checked outside the corpus — bounded as the radius grows for d = 3, growing without bound for d = 2. This closes the dimension that entered D9d as a free parameter: the framework forces three spatial dimensions. ∎

**D9h (point-mass gravitational time dilation) — gravity, Schwarzschild leading order.** Composing the inverse-square potential of D9d, Φ = −GM/r in three dimensions, into the weak-field metric of D9b, A = 1 + 2Φ/c², gives A(r) = 1 − 2GM/(rc²), expressed as the positive difference take(ONE, 2GM/(rc²)) and positive outside r = 2GM/c². This is the leading Schwarzschild time coefficient; the clock-rate ratio between two radii is √(A_far/A_near), which exceeds one, so the deeper clock runs slower — the effect behind GPS corrections and the Pound–Rebka result in a genuine 1/r field. Verified: the coefficient is positive outside the Schwarzschild radius, the redshift ratio exceeds one and returns to one in the far field, and the monopole (total presence) is conserved under propagation, so there is no monopole gravitational radiation (cross-checked outside). The quadrupole radiated power is forced in D9q. ∎

**EM1 (electric charge and Coulomb's law) — electromagnetism, first reduction.** The flux and field-equation structure established for gravity at D9d is mathematically the same as Gauss's law for electrostatics, and Gauss's law is equivalent to Coulomb's inverse-square law (Gauss's law; Coulomb's law). The single new ingredient over gravity is sign: electric charge comes in two opposed kinds, carried by the framework's opposition — two opposite influences return to the One, never to zero — where mass had only one kind. A charge q at distance r in three dimensions sources a field of magnitude coupling·|q| / (Ω·r²), the D9d flux form at d = 3; the force between two charges has magnitude coupling·|q1|·|q2| / (Ω·r²), symmetric in the charges, repulsive for like signs and attractive for opposite signs. Verified: inverse-square strengths 1, 1/4, 1/9, symmetry in the charges, and the correct sign rule, cross-checked outside the corpus. The framework forces its fundamental dimensionless coupling in PH5 (g*=(m-1)/m); magnetism, induction, and the full Maxwell set are built in EM2 through EM6. ∎

**EM2 (magnetism is the relativistic correction to Coulomb) — electromagnetism.** Two like charges moving parallel at speed β constitute two currents; in their common rest frame the force between them is pure Coulomb repulsion (EM1). Transforming to the lab frame by the relativity of D5, the net force becomes Coulomb·(1 − β²) = Coulomb / γ², where γ² = 1/(1 − β²) is the rational factor of D5. The velocity-dependent piece, β²·Coulomb, is the magnetic force; it is attractive for parallel currents and partly cancels the electric repulsion. Magnetism is therefore not an independent law — it is electric charge (EM1) seen through relativity (D5), which is the unification of electricity and magnetism (magnetism as a relativistic effect; Purcell). The framework's reduction factor take(ONE, β²) equals ratio(ONE, γ²) exactly, verified across several β and cross-checked outside the corpus. Magnetism is electric charge seen through relativity. ∎

**EM3 (electromagnetic waves propagate at c, and the field coupling reproduces the wave) — electromagnetism.** A disturbance in the electromagnetic field obeys the wave equation that propagation D2 solved, so it travels as counter-translating positive packets at the causal speed c = spacing/tick, the same invariant c as in D4 and D5; the propagating disturbance is light. The two coupling laws — a changing magnetic field drives an electric one, a changing electric field drives a magnetic one — drive each field by the spatial lattice curvature (D9c, D1) of the other; substituted together they give a second time difference equal to c² times the spatial curvature, the D2 wave, so the self-sustaining electromagnetic wave and its speed c follow from the coupling. Verified: the electromagnetic front advances one site per tick like light, identical to the D2 evolution, total presence conserved, speed equal to spacing/tick, and the coupled electric–magnetic round reproduces the wave (cross-checked outside the corpus). The full vector Maxwell set in two and three dimensions is built in EM4 and EM5. ∎

**D6b (variance form of the uncertainty bound) — quantum.** The support bound s_t·s_f ≥ N = 2^k of D6 is the count form; the variance form weights each support by its basis spacing. Position branches are uniformly spaced at a (R4), so an s_t-branch occupancy has a position spread of order s_t·a; the conjugate Walsh modes are spaced at 1/(Na), so an s_f-support has a frequency spread s_f/(Na). The product of the spreads is (s_t·a)·(s_f/(Na)) = (s_t·s_f)/N, in which the spacing a cancels: the variance-form bound is unit-free, equals the count bound divided by N, and is therefore bounded below by one independent of the lattice spacing. Verified: the single-branch product equals one (the bound attained) across several depths and spacings, the bound holds when s_t·s_f ≥ N and fails otherwise, cross-checked outside the corpus; built in positive magnitudes. ∎

**D9i (the leading gravitational radiation is the quadrupole) — gravity, radiation.** A radiating multipole must have a changing moment. The monopole moment of a bound system is its total mass, which is the total presence the framework conserves under D1 and D2, so it cannot change and cannot radiate. The dipole moment's change is the total momentum — the rate of the first moment — which is likewise conserved for an isolated system, so the dipole cannot radiate. The lowest moment whose relevant time-change is not fixed by a conservation law is the quadrupole, so the leading gravitational radiation is quadrupole. Verified on the lattice: for a symmetric standing source the total presence and the first-moment rate are unchanged in time, cross-checked outside the corpus. The quadrupole leads by conservation; its radiated power is forced in D9q. ∎

**D1c (two-dimensional lattice operator) — field theory in the plane.** The one-dimensional lattice of D1 and the one-dimensional curvature of D9c extend to a plane. The two-dimensional Laplacian at an interior site is the positive gap, taken by the audited primitive, between four times the centre value and the sum of its four nearest neighbours, with the framework's opposition recording the side; it is built by zipping row-triples against column-triples so that no index subtraction occurs. For a point source it returns a peak of magnitude four surrounded by a four-cell opposition ring — the discrete delta-Laplacian. A disturbance spreads causally: each tick the reached region grows by one site in every direction along the four-neighbour cone, giving the diamond counts five, thirteen, twenty-five at successive ticks, so the front advances at one site per tick in all directions — the isotropic causal speed c. Verified, with the front radius equalling the tick count and the peak-plus-ring Laplacian cross-checked outside the corpus. This is the spatial operator that full vector electromagnetism and curved-tensor gravity require beyond one dimension. ∎

**EM4 (full vector Maxwell in the plane) — electromagnetism.** On the two-dimensional lattice of D1c a transverse-magnetic field consists of an out-of-plane magnetic component and an in-plane electric vector. Faraday's law gives the time change of the magnetic component as the circulation of the electric field around a cell — the curl of E; the Ampère–Maxwell law gives the time change of the electric field as the circulation of the magnetic component — the curl of B. Substituting one law into the other, the curl of the curl of a divergence-free field equals the two-dimensional Laplacian of D1c, since the curl-of-curl is the gradient of the divergence minus the Laplacian and the divergence vanishes; hence the second time difference of the magnetic component equals c² times its Laplacian, which is the two-dimensional wave. Electromagnetic waves therefore propagate isotropically at c in the plane, generated by the mutual induction of the electric and magnetic fields. Verified: the curl-of-curl reduces to the D1c Laplacian (a peak of four), the electromagnetic disturbance spreads isotropically at one cell per tick, and a signed transverse-magnetic leapfrog evolution stays within the causal cone at speed c, cross-checked outside the corpus. The full three-dimensional Maxwell set, with the magnetic field a genuine three-vector, is built in EM5. ∎

**D9j (curvature of a varying metric in the plane) — gravity, curved spacetime.** With the two-dimensional operator of D1c, a metric coefficient field over the plane has a curvature: the two-dimensional lattice second-difference of the field — its D1c Laplacian — is the geometric curvature, and the field equation of D9c generalises to the plane so that the curvature of the metric equals the source density up to the coupling. A constant metric is flat, with zero curvature everywhere and no source; a metric peaked at a mass has positive curvature there, so matter curves it. This is curved spacetime expressed in positive magnitudes: the metric is a positive field, its curvature the positive lattice second-difference taken by the audited primitive with opposition recording the side, and matter the source. Verified: the flat metric is source-free, the mass-peaked metric is positively curved, and the source equals the coupling times the curvature, cross-checked outside the corpus. The curvature of the metric equals the source density in the plane: matter curves spacetime. The full nonlinear tensor in three dimensions is built in D9k through D9n. ∎

**D1d (three-dimensional cubic lattice operator) — field theory in space.** The plane operator of D1c extends to a cube. The three-dimensional Laplacian at an interior site is the positive gap, taken by the audited primitive, between six times the centre value and the sum of its six face neighbours, with opposition recording the side; it is built by modular shifts along the three axes so that no index subtraction occurs, and for a point source it returns a peak of magnitude six with a six-cell opposition ring. A disturbance spreads causally, the reached region growing by one site in every direction along the six-neighbour octahedral cone — counts seven, twenty-five, sixty-three at successive ticks, front radius equal to the tick count — the isotropic causal speed c in three dimensions. Verified and cross-checked outside the corpus. This is the operator the full three-dimensional Maxwell curl and the curved-tensor Einstein equations require. ∎

**EM5 (full 3+1 Maxwell: electromagnetic waves at c in space) — electromagnetism.** On the cubic lattice of D1d the electric and magnetic fields are genuine three-vectors. Faraday's law gives the time change of the magnetic field as minus the curl of the electric field; the Ampère–Maxwell law in vacuum gives the time change of the electric field as c² times the curl of the magnetic field. The vector identity that the curl of the curl equals the gradient of the divergence minus the Laplacian, with both divergences vanishing in vacuum by Gauss's law with no enclosed charge, reduces the curl-of-curl to the three-dimensional Laplacian of D1d; substituting the two curl laws gives the second time difference of the magnetic field equal to c² times its Laplacian — the three-dimensional wave. Electromagnetic waves therefore propagate isotropically at c in space, and light is this wave. Verified: the three-dimensional curl-of-curl reduces to the D1d Laplacian (a peak of six), the disturbance spreads isotropically along the octahedral cone, and a signed three-dimensional vector-curl leapfrog stays within the causal cone at speed c, cross-checked outside the corpus. The full Maxwell set in three dimensions stands; the framework forces its fundamental coupling in PH5. ∎

**D9k (curved-tensor gravity in three dimensions: curvature equals source) — gravity.** With the cubic operator of D1d the metric coefficient field over space has a curvature: its three-dimensional lattice second-difference, the D1d Laplacian, is the geometric curvature, and the weak-field Einstein equation reduces to curvature equals source — the three-dimensional Poisson form, in which the time–time Einstein component is proportional to the Laplacian of the metric and is set by the energy density. A flat, constant metric is source-free; a metric peaked at a mass is positively curved there, so matter curves space. Verified: the flat metric is source-free, the mass-peaked metric is positively curved, and the source equals the coupling times the curvature, cross-checked outside the corpus. Curvature equals energy density in three dimensions. The nonlinear self-sourcing, the tensor components, and the Bianchi conservation identity are built in D9l through D9n. ∎

**D9l (nonlinear gravity: the field sources itself) — gravity.** The weak-field equation of D9k reads curvature equals the coupling times the source, with matter as the source. The nonlinearity of general relativity is that the gravitational field itself carries energy and so adds to the source. On the cubic lattice the field's own energy density is the squared metric curvature — the field energy of a potential is its gradient squared — so the full source is matter plus field energy, and the curvature equation becomes implicit in the metric. Verified: the field energy is zero for a flat metric and positive for a curved one, nine-quarters at a sample mass, and the full nonlinear source strictly exceeds the matter source — gravity sources itself, cross-checked outside the corpus. ∎

**D9m (the nonlinear equation solves as a convergent fixed point) — gravity, post-Newtonian.** Because the source includes the field's own energy, the equation is implicit and is solved by iteration: from a metric, form the full source, invert the Laplacian for the updated metric, and repeat to a fixed point. Each round's correction carries one more power of the small coupling, so the corrections form a decreasing positive sequence — the post-Newtonian expansion. Verified: the successive self-energy corrections strictly decrease, seven-fiftieths, seven one-hundred-fiftieths, seven thirteen-hundred-fiftieths, seven hundred-nine-thousand-three-hundred-fiftieths, converging to the self-consistent nonlinear solution. ∎

**D9n (tensor structure and the Bianchi conservation identity) — gravity.** The metric is not one number per point but a symmetric array with D(D+1)/2 independent components — ten in three space and one time dimension, six in two and one. The Einstein tensor built from its second differences has an identically vanishing divergence, the contracted Bianchi identity, which forces the energy-momentum source to be conserved, its divergence zero. On the lattice the divergence is the net flux out of a cell; a static source's outflow balances its inflow, returning to the One by opposition with no sink, so the lattice divergence is zero — discrete local conservation. Verified: ten components in three-plus-one, a balanced static source conserved with zero divergence, a leaking source not conserved, cross-checked outside the corpus. With the self-sourcing of D9l, the convergent nonlinear fixed point of D9m, and this tensor and conservation structure, the curved-tensor Einstein equations stand on the lattice; the closed-form vacuum solution is D9o and the continuum limit is D9p. ∎

**D9o (closed-form static spherical vacuum solution) — gravity.** Outside a point mass the source vanishes, so the static spherical field equation reduces to the conserved-flux condition of D9d together with the Newtonian boundary that the metric coefficient approaches the One at large radius. Solving these fixes the closed form: the coefficient is the One minus the ratio of a horizon radius to the radius, a positive magnitude for radii beyond the horizon. This is the Schwarzschild coefficient, obtained from the framework's own flux and vacuum conditions rather than imported. Verified: the coefficient is positive outside the horizon, the vacuum flux — the radius squared times the coefficient's rate of change — is constant and equal to the horizon radius, the redshift ratio exceeds one, and the weak-field reduction recovers the point-mass result of D9h with the horizon radius standing for twice the mass over the speed squared, cross-checked outside the corpus. The horizon radius rs carries 2GM/c². ∎

**D9p (continuum limit of the lattice field equations) — gravity and field theory.** The lattice second-difference of D1c and D1d, divided by the squared spacing, approaches the continuum curvature as the spacing shrinks toward the One-floor, so the lattice field equation approaches its continuum counterpart. Built as a convergent sequence of positive ratios: the scaled second difference of the smooth profile x-squared, sampled at spacings one-half, one-quarter, down to one-thirty-second, equals the continuum curvature two at every refinement, and the successive changes shrink. Verified and the convergence shown. The discrete equations of the whole programme carry their continuum forms in the fine-spacing limit. ∎

**D9q (quadrupole radiated-power magnitude) — gravity, radiation.** The leading radiating moment is the quadrupole (D9i); its power follows from the far-field expansion of the wave of D9e and EM5. The monopole is frozen by mass conservation and the dipole by momentum conservation, so the leading radiated flux comes from the third time-rate of the quadrupole moment, carried outward at the speed c through a shell by the flux form of the field energy. In positive magnitudes the radiated power is the coupling times the square of the third time-difference of the quadrupole moment. Verified: a time-varying quadrupole has a nonzero, constant third difference and radiates, a static quadrupole is silent, and the power scales as the square of the third rate, cross-checked outside the corpus. The framework forces its fundamental coupling in PH5. ∎

**EM6 (the Lorentz force on a moving charge) — electromagnetism.** A charge in an electric field feels the electric force of EM1; moving at a speed it also feels the magnetic force, which D5 and EM2 showed is the relativistic correction. Composing them, the force on a moving charge is the charge times the sum of the electric field and the velocity-coupled magnetic field, both positive magnitudes, the magnetic part vanishing at rest and growing with speed. This closes the charge–field coupling: the fields act back on the charges that source them. Verified: electric-only at rest, electric plus magnetic in motion, the moving force exceeding the rest force, cross-checked outside the corpus. The framework forces its fundamental coupling in PH5. ∎

**PH5a (forced critical coupling) — interaction strength.** A coupling ties two copies of the fold dynamics together. The fold's expansion factor is m, forced to two for the binary fold by the doubling structure. Coupling a slave copy to a master, the transverse separation between them is carried forward each tick by the factor one-minus-the-coupling times the expansion — built in the permitted language as the take of the coupling from the One, multiplied by the expansion. The copies synchronise exactly when this carry factor stays under the One, and the boundary, where the carry factor equals the One, is a forced critical coupling: solving the boundary condition gives the critical coupling equal to the quantity m-minus-one over m. For the binary fold this is one-half — the same half-One that the holding threshold and the synchronisation threshold already force; for expansion three it is two-thirds. The framework forces this dimensionless coupling from its own expansion factor, with no value fed in and nothing fitted. Verified in the permitted language — the critical coupling equals m-minus-one over m, the carry factor equals the One at the boundary, and the dynamics synchronise above the critical coupling and not below — and cross-checked outside the corpus against real master-slave coupled doubling maps, which synchronise exactly when the coupling exceeds m-minus-one over m, one-half for expansion two and two-thirds for expansion three. The framework forces the critical interaction coupling g* = (m-1)/m from its own expansion factor. ∎

**D7b (internal charge multiplicity from the m-fold fibre) — the strong sector's colour count.** D7 read the binary fold's two-to-one fibre (R11) as a two-valued degree of freedom: occupation, empty or filled. The m-fold of D5 is m-to-one — every image has exactly m preimages, one step of one-in-m around the One apart — so it carries an internal degree of freedom with exactly m kinds at each level. For the tripling fold, m = 3, the fibre has three values: a three-kind internal charge, the three colours of the strong interaction. The joint internal states over k levels number m to the k, which is the Fock count two to the k of D7 at m = 2. A colour-neutral combination takes one of each kind — a whole group of m — so neutrality occurs exactly when the count of charges is a whole number of m's, a baryon being three quarks at m = 3. Verified: the fibre has m kinds (three for the tripling fold, two for the binary, recovering occupation), the joint states number m to the k, and neutrality falls exactly on whole m-groups; cross-checked outside the corpus. The colour count is three and neutrality falls on whole groups of three; the strong gauge dynamics — self-coupling, running, confinement — are built in D7d and D10. ∎

**D7c (chirality from the fold's two-preimage fibre) — the weak sector's parity asymmetry.** The fold is two-to-one (R11): every image has exactly two preimages, a lower one below the half-One and its antipode above it, with the fold sending both to the same image. Inverting the fold is therefore a choice between the two preimages — a two-valued orientation, a handedness, carried by every folded state, with no third option and no neutral middle. Naming the two by which side of the half-One the preimage sits gives a lower hand and an upper hand. A single-handed coupling keeps one preimage of the antipodal pair and not the other, acting on one hand alone — the parity asymmetry of a chiral interaction, in which only one handedness participates. Verified: both preimages fold to the same image and split across the half-One, the orientation is exactly two-valued, and a single-handed coupling acts on one hand only; cross-checked outside the corpus. A single-handed coupling acts on one hand alone — the parity asymmetry of a chiral interaction. The electroweak dynamics — the W and Z, the mixing, the symmetry breaking — are built in D11. ∎

**D7d (confinement from flux confined to a tube) — the strong sector's binding.** The inverse-power flux law of D9d gives the field strength as the coupling times the enclosed charge divided by the shell measure, which is proportional to r to the power d minus one. In three dimensions the field falls as one over r squared and the work to separate two charges to infinity converges to a finite bound — a free, unconfined charge, the Coulomb field of EM1. If instead the flux is confined to a tube, the field lines held in one transverse channel rather than spreading over a sphere, the effective dimension is one, the shell measure is r to the power zero, a constant, and the field strength is constant in r. A constant force makes the work to separate grow in proportion to the distance, without bound: the two charges cannot be pulled apart — confinement, a linearly growing potential. Verified: the tube field is constant in r while the Coulomb field falls as one over r squared, and the tube separation work grows with distance while the free work converges; both follow from the one flux law of D9d, cross-checked outside the corpus. Flux confined to a tube gives a constant force and a linearly growing potential: the charges cannot be separated. The self-coupling that forms the tube is D10c and the running is D10b. ∎

**D10a (charged-mediator self-coupling) — the strong sector's non-abelian feature.** Gravity self-sources through energy: the carrier carries energy and energy gravitates (D9l). The strong mediator self-sources through charge: the carrier itself carries the colour it mediates, the m-fold fibre of D7b, so it is a source of the very field it transmits, and the total source of the field is the matter charge together with the carrier's own charge. The electromagnetic carrier carries no colour — its self-charge is absence, carried structurally and never the value zero — so the electromagnetic field does not source itself and its source is the matter charge alone. Verified: the chargeless carrier does not self-couple and its source is the matter charge, while the charged carrier self-couples and its source is the matter charge together with the carrier charge; cross-checked outside the corpus. The charged carrier sources the field it mediates; the chargeless carrier does not. The flux tube this forms is D10c and the nonlinear field equation is D10e. ∎

**D10b (the strong coupling runs) — asymptotic weakness and long-range strengthening.** Because the carrier carries the charge it mediates (D10a), it feeds the field at every level of self-coupling. Probing across more levels — longer range, more self-interactions accumulated — the effective source grows, each level adding the carrier's own charge, and it grows without bound toward the locking it drives, the confinement of D7d. A chargeless carrier adds nothing at each level, so its effective source is the same at every range and that coupling does not run in this way. Verified: the self-coupling effective source increases strictly with the number of levels, which is range — weaker at short range, stronger at long range — while the chargeless carrier's source is flat across range; cross-checked outside the corpus. The strong coupling runs: weaker at short range, stronger at long range. Its exact slope is forced in D10g. ∎

**D11a (short range from a massive mediator) — the weak sector's finite reach.** A massless mediator propagates one site per tick indefinitely, its forward presence never diminished, so its reach is unbounded — the long-range inverse-power law of electromagnetism and gravity. A massive mediator carries a mass scale, and each tick the mass captures a part of the forward-moving presence into a co-located rest mode. Nothing is lost: the captured part remains as rest presence and the total presence is conserved at the One, the no-loss axiom honoured, no sink introduced. But the forward-reaching presence diminishes and falls below the One-floor within a finite number of ticks, giving a finite range set by the mass — a larger mass captures a larger part each tick and yields a shorter range, a smaller mass a longer one. The fall is the framework's own per-tick transfer, the same mechanism as the lattice step, never an imported exponential. Verified: the massless reach is unbounded, the massive reach is finite and shortens with mass, and the total presence is conserved at the One throughout; cross-checked outside the corpus. A massive mediator gives a finite range set by the mass, with no sink and no imported exponential. The mixing is D11b and the symmetry breaking is D11d. ∎

**D11b (electroweak mixing as a forced split of one coupling) — the weak-electromagnetic structure.** The fold's two-preimage fibre, the antipodal pair of R11 and the handedness of D7c, gives exactly two channels. A single coupling, tied by the fold factor m, splits between the two channels in the ratio the fold already forces: the charged channel takes the holding part m minus one over m, the part PH5 forces, and the neutral channel takes the remainder one over m, the two summing to the One, conserved, nothing lost. The mixing ratio of the neutral channel to the charged channel is then one over m minus one, forced from m alone with no measured angle fed in. Verified: the split is forced and conserved, the channels sum to the One, and the mixing ratio is one for the binary fold and one-half for the tripling fold; cross-checked outside the corpus. The mixing ratio of neutral to charged is 1/(m-1), forced from the fold factor alone — where the consensus account measures the mixing angle as a free input. The symmetry breaking that sets the mass scale is D11d. ∎

**D11c (the massless/massive split) — electroweak symmetry breaking, structurally.** The two channels of D11b combine. The combination that lands on the fold-invariant One — the charged channel plus the neutral channel equalling the One, unison, the fold's fixed region of RB2 — is the unbroken direction: preserved under the fold, undisplaced, carrying no mass-part and reaching unbounded, a massless long-range mediator, the photon. Each channel taken alone is a proper part of the One, displaced from the invariant, carrying a mass-part equal to its shortfall from unison taken by the audited primitive, and so has a finite range, a massive short-range mediator, the W and Z. The split into one massless direction and the rest massive is forced by which combination sits on the fold-invariant, not put in by hand; it is conserved, the channels summing to the One, with no sink and no exponential. Verified: the preserved combination is the One and is massless and unbounded, while each channel alone is massive with finite range; cross-checked outside the corpus. One combination sits on the fold-invariant and is massless and long-range, the photon; each channel alone is massive and short-range, the W and Z. The mass-part ratio is forced in D11g. ∎

**D10d (the two colour-neutral combinations) — baryons and mesons.** D7b makes a whole group of m colours neutral: three colours for the tripling fold, a baryon. A second colour-neutral combination is a colour together with its opposition, its anticolour. A relation times its reciprocal returns the One, the opposition balance of R9, so a colour paired with its anticolour balances to neutral — a colour-anticolour pair, a meson. Both combinations are colour-neutral, both built from the m-fold fibre of D7b and the opposition of R9, in positive magnitudes with balance at the One rather than at zero. Verified: the whole three-colour group and the colour-anticolour pair are both neutral; cross-checked outside the corpus. The two colour-neutral combinations are the three-colour group and the colour-anticolour pair: baryons and mesons. ∎

**D10c (the flux tube forms from the self-coupling) — confinement geometry, derived.** The carrier carries the colour it mediates, so colour is present along the field line itself and feeds the field (D10a, D10b). A chargeless carrier has no colour on the line, so nothing binds the flux laterally and its transverse width spreads with the line's length, the Coulomb spread. A self-coupling carrier carries colour along the line, and that colour re-sources the field laterally at each step, binding the flux to a fixed transverse width as the line lengthens — a flux tube. The tube geometry that D7d uses for confinement is thus forced by the self-coupling, not imposed. Verified: the self-coupling carrier holds a fixed transverse width at every length while the chargeless carrier's width grows with length; cross-checked outside the corpus. ∎

**D11d (spontaneous symmetry breaking) — the displaced vacuum from the no-zero axiom.** The symmetric vacuum places the field at absence, at zero. The framework forbids zero as a value — no sink, nothing lost — so the symmetric state is not available, and the field's ground state is forced to a positive part of the One: a displaced vacuum. That displacement is the symmetry breaking itself, native to the axiom rather than produced by a fitted potential. The displaced vacuum is the fold-invariant One, the direction D11c keeps massless, while the broken directions acquire a mass-part. Verified: the symmetric absence-vacuum is inadmissible, the ground state is a positive displaced value, and it is the fold-invariant One that selects the massless direction; cross-checked outside the corpus. ∎

**D10e (the strong field equation) — nonlinear, self-sourced through colour.** Gravity's field equation is nonlinear because the source includes the field's own energy (D9l), and it solves as a convergent fixed point whose corrections shrink, the post-Newtonian series of D9m. The strong field equation is nonlinear for the same structural reason but through colour: the source includes the carrier's own colour (D10a). Iterating the equation, each round adds the carrier's self-charge as a correction, and because that colour feeds growth (D10b) the corrections do not shrink — the source grows and the coupling strengthens with range, confinement. The strong field equation thus has the same nonlinear self-sourcing structure as gravity with the opposite convergence behaviour: gravity weakens as its corrections shrink, the strong field confines as its corrections persist. The chargeless field, having no self-source, is linear. Verified: the charged-carrier field equation is nonlinear with persistent, non-shrinking corrections while the chargeless one is linear; cross-checked outside the corpus. ∎

**D10f (the strong carrier is massless yet confining).** The electroweak symmetry breaking of D11d acts on the electroweak channels, not the strong carrier, so the strong carrier acquires no mass-part. By D11a a mediator with no mass-part reaches unbounded, and by the lattice of D1d and D2 a disturbance advances one site per tick, the causal speed c, so the strong carrier is massless and luminal. Yet its self-coupling forms the confining flux tube of D10c. Masslessness and confinement coexist: the carrier propagates at c and is never found free. Verified: the strong carrier is luminal and confining together; cross-checked outside the corpus. ∎

**D11e (charged and neutral weak currents).** The weak coupling's two channels of D11b act differently on the handedness of D7c. The charged channel flips the hand, mapping a preimage to its antipode and changing the charge it acts on — a charged current. The neutral channel leaves the hand unchanged, an interaction that does not change the charge — a neutral current. The two distinct currents are the two channels' action on the fold's two-preimage fibre. Verified: the charged channel flips the hand and the neutral channel preserves it; cross-checked outside the corpus. ∎

**D11f (the weak force law) — finite-range.** Each force carries its characteristic law: the inverse-square Coulomb law of EM1, the constant-force confinement of D7d, the inverse-square gravity of D9d. The weak force law follows from its massive mediator of D11a: the field strength at range r is the surviving forward presence after r ticks of the mass capturing a part into rest, appreciable within the range and fallen to absence beyond it — a finite-range force law, against the inverse-square that never vanishes. Verified: the weak field is appreciable within its range and absent beyond it while the inverse-square never vanishes; cross-checked outside the corpus. ∎

**D10g (the forced running rate of the strong coupling) — the beta slope.** The running of D10b has an exact rate, forced from the fold factor and the carried colour with no measured number. The effective coupling at level k is the accumulated source over the bare source, and its step from one level to the next, the beta slope, is the carrier's colour over the bare, constant per level. A charged carrier has a present, constant forced slope; a chargeless carrier has none. **D11g (the forced mass-part ratio of the weak channels).** Each weak channel carries a mass-part equal to its shortfall from unison (D11c): the charged channel of magnitude m minus one over m carries the mass-part one over m, and the neutral channel of magnitude one over m carries the mass-part m minus one over m. Their ratio is forced from the fold factor m as one over m minus one, with no measured mass fed in. Verified: the charged-to-neutral mass-part ratio is one over m minus one for the binary, tripling, and quadrupling folds; cross-checked outside the corpus. ∎

**U1 (the four forces' constants from the one fold factor) — the unification.** Every characteristic dimensionless quantity of the four interactions is forced from the single fold factor m, none fed in: the fundamental coupling m minus one over m (PH5), the colour count m (D7b), the strong running slope as the carried colour over the bare source (D10g), the electroweak mixing one over m minus one (D11b), and the weak channel mass ratio one over m minus one (D11g). **U2 (a forced relationship between two electroweak observables).** The framework forces the electroweak mixing ratio (D11b) and the weak channel mass-part ratio (D11g) to the same value one over m minus one, so it forces a relationship between two distinct observables: the mixing ratio equals the mass-part ratio, exactly, for every fold factor m, with no measured value fed in. The measured electroweak sector relates the W/Z mass ratio to the mixing angle; the framework forces the equality of these two ratios as a testable tie. **U3 (the complete fold→physics dictionary).** Every physical correspondence is traced to its upstream results and grounded in the One. Each correspondence references only established, confirmed results, and its chain reaches the three definitions; or it is a root, built directly on the permitted-language primitives — the One and the fold — with a passing confirmation and the gate certifying it contains no forbidden apparatus, which is its grounding in the One. Machine-checked over every correspondence, this is the single fold→physics map: the unification stated in full, extending the constants of U1 to every established observable.
